		node.parentNode.insertBefore(gads, node);
		})();
	</script>

<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}

The design is optimized to operate at 0.945, 2.50, 3.50, and 5.80 GHz using the finite element method. In this design, two U-shaped, two F-shaped, and four L-shaped branches are used as additional resonators to achieve multiband operation. Simulated results show that the 30 Ã30-mm<sup>2</sup> antenna achieves less than -10 dB reflection coefficient at the targeted frequencies. Measured results are given to validate the antenna's performance. Although the proposed antenna attenuates a bit at some frequencies, measured S<sub>11</sub> is less than -6.5 dB at all frequencies, and it is less than -19 dB at 2.50 GHz.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Wireless communication applications such as radio frequency identification (RFID), Worldwide Interoperability for Microwave Access (WiMAX), and wireless local area network (WLAN) technologies have been widely used. For instance, RFID has been applied to supply chain management, access control, patient identification, suitcase security, tracking in airport luggage operations, and so on <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>. The operating frequency is available for these applications at different bands. RFID operation is usually assigned at 0.92/2.45/5.8-GHz bands; WiMAX is allocated the 2.5/3.5/5.5-GHz bands, and WLAN is allocated the 2.4/5.2/5.8Â GHz bands. Recently, it has become a tendency to design an antenna that can operate at multiple frequency bands since different standards may be used simultaneously in one system. Some triple-band antennas have been designed for RFID or WiMAX/WLAN applications, respectively. Planar inverted-F antenna (PIFA) (433Â MHz/912Â MHz/2.45Â GHz) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a> and meandered dipole antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a> (0.92/2.45/5.8Â GHz) are reported as RFID triple-band antennas. Triple-band antennas <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a> operating at 2.45/3.5/5.5-GHz bands are presented for WiMAX or WLAN applications. However, to the best knowledge of the authors, there is not a single antenna reported to cover bands for RFID/WiMAX/WLAN applications.</p><p>In this letter, to meet the multiband requirement, a novel four-band coplanar waveguide (CPW)-fed folded slot monopole antenna is proposed that is suitable for the 0.94/2.45/5.8-GHz RFID tag and 2.45/3.5/5.5-GHz WiMAX/WLAN applications. The performance of the antenna is validated using finite element method (FEM), method of moments (MOM), and measured results. Simulation results, including the reflection coefficients, radiation patterns, and antenna gains at the specified frequency bands, are discussed.</p></div>

In order to achieve multiband performance, the designed symmetric antenna has two U-shaped, four L-shaped, and two F-shaped branches. The six branches function as additional resonators to resonate the antenna at multiple frequency bands. The measured peak antenna gains are â3.75, â2.79, 9.57, and 9.19Â dBi at 0.945, 2.50, 3.52, and 5.80Â GHz, respectively. Two methods are used in the numerical analysis, which are FEM and MOM. It can be seen that gains simulated by FEM are higher than MOM results at most of frequencies, and measured gains at three frequencies are higher than the corresponding gains simulated by FEM and MOM. All the measured and simulated gains have the same tendency at different frequencies. The reason why the gain is low at 0.945Â GHz is because the ground plane is small in terms of wavelength. Therefore, the actual slot is equal to 0.65 times of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-91-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-871" role="math" style="display: inline-block; This situation is similar to the literature <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_3">[11]</a> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_3">[12]</a>. The measured gain is low for the lowest frequency, which is expected due to the small size of the antenna as compared to its size at 3.5 and 5.8Â GHz <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_3">[11]</a>. We have also found that many previous works <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_3">[13]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_3">[14]</a> on multiband antenna have rather different gains at different frequency. For instance, measured gains in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_3">[14]</a> are â6, â4, 2.5, 5, and 4Â dBi at 1.5, 3, 5.5, 9.5, and 11Â GHz, respectively. Nevertheless, these antennas could play a role in many applications in some ways. If the proposed antenna is applied on an RFID application, it may be suitable for an RFID tag antenna, and the corresponding RFID reader may use frequency hopping from 860Â to 960Â MHz.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A novel four-band RFID tag antenna is reported in this letter. Two U-shaped, two F-shaped, and four L-shaped branches are utilized as additional resonators in order to achieve multiband operation. Measured results are given to validate the design. In the future, by adjusting parameters <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-93-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-879" role="math" style="display: inline-block; Moreover, the distance from slot <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-95-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-895" role="math" style="display: inline-block; <script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
